Please note: (Coal) from the ground to the freight car and back, 9 cents per metric ton; from the warehouse or freight car to the deck of the ship or barge, or to the crane hook on the ship, and back, 1 jiao per metric ton; unloading 70 to 150-ton barges, 6 yuan 5 jiao to 13 yuan per boat; unloading 150 to 100-ton barges, 13 yuan to 26 yuan per boat; unloading 200-ton or heavier barges, 30 yuan per boat; direct transfer of coal from the ship's hold to the car, or from the ship's hold to the car yard and then onto the car, 3 jiao 8 fen per ton. (Goods) from the warehouse or freight car to the deck of the ship or barge, or to the crane hook on the ship, and back, 1 jiao 4 fen per metric ton; from the warehouse to the freight car and back, 1 jiao 4 fen per metric ton; moving from one section of the warehouse to another, or from one warehouse to another, 6 fen per metric ton; moving for re-weighing and customs inspection, 1 fen per bag. (Sesame and beans) re-bagging, adding marks, and sealing the bag, and weighing, etc., 1 fen per bag; drying, sifting, cleaning, adding marks, sealing the bag, and weighing, etc., if soil and dirt need to be removed, they must be cleaned, 3 fen per 50 jin or less than 50 kilograms; cleaning with machinery, drying, sifting, cleaning, adding marks, sealing the bag, and weighing, etc., if soil and dirt need to be removed, they must be cleaned, 2 fen per 50 jin or less than 50 kilograms. Attention Should be Paid to Disinfection Procedures for Cholera Vaccination 154

Notice from the Municipal Health Bureau

The Municipal Health Bureau issued a notice yesterday, stating that the Bureau is promoting free cholera vaccination to protect the health of citizens, increase their resistance to cholera bacteria, and prevent the spread of cholera. The vaccination method is carried out in accordance with the medical procedures, and there is no negligence due to the fact that it is free. Therefore, the personnel sent to carry out the vaccination have considerable knowledge and experience, and the disinfection procedures are already clear. The following procedures must be followed during vaccination: (1) Before the vaccination begins, the syringes and needles must be boiled and sterilized. (2) Used needles should be disinfected in alcohol. (3) The skin on the outside of the upper arm should be wiped with alcohol for disinfection before subcutaneous injection. (4) A new needle should be used for each person vaccinated, and the alcohol in the needle should be removed when attaching the needle. (5) After the vaccination is completed, the instruments should be cleaned, and the needles should be immersed in ether. (6) The number of vaccinated people and the vaccination personnel must fill out an examination form, and the group going to vaccinate must stamp it for verification by the Bureau. The methods are thorough and are supervised and verified at all times. Over the years, more than 1.1 million citizens have benefited from the various vaccinations carried out. It has been found that one or two newspapers have suggested that the health administrative authorities should inform the vaccination personnel to pay attention to disinfection when giving injections. However, the Public Health Department of the International Settlement and the Health Bureau of the French Concession have also been promoting free vaccinations this year. It is not known what the health administrative authorities mentioned by the newspapers refer to, and there is no basis for verification. In addition to informing the vaccination personnel of the Bureau that the above-mentioned disinfection procedures must be strictly followed during vaccination, citizens may report any negligence or failure to disinfect at any time for verification. However, it has been heard that one or two places have disregarded the epidemic prevention of workers and prevented them from being vaccinated, and the health administrative authorities have reprimanded them, or that rumors have been deliberately created to evade responsibility. It is also possible that my citizens are aware that the work of the Bureau is completely based on protecting the health of citizens and preventing the harm of cholera. Although the vaccination is free, the handling is still very cautious. Everyone is encouraged to receive the vaccination actively and not be deceived, so as to prevent the harm of the epidemic. After the vaccination, the injection site may be slightly swollen and uncomfortable due to the action of the vaccine, but it will recover quickly and there is no harm. Please do not misunderstand. This notice.

News from the Township Poor People's Loan Office 157

In order to help poor people borrow capital to make a living and solve their livelihood problems, the Municipal Social Bureau established a loan office in Minli Road in Zhabei and Zhonghua Road in the South City last year. Poor people who went to borrow capital were very enthusiastic. With the approval of the Municipal Government, 10,000 yuan was allocated to open offices in various townships. Farmers in various townships have always borrowed money, but they could only mortgage to wealthy households, and the interest rates were very high. Since the establishment of the loan office, agricultural loans can be borrowed for 15 yuan, and poor people can borrow for 10 yuan, with interest rates ranging from 8 to 6 percent (weekly interest). Therefore, the poor farmers have obtained this low-interest loan institution, and they have

submitted requests for loans. Therefore, the total number of loans in Gaoqiao and Yinhang districts has reached the maximum limit, and the loans in other districts such as Wusong, Zhenru, and Luhang have also reached 1,000 yuan. It is heard that farmers in Gaoqiao district are still submitting requests for loans, so they have requested the Bureau to increase the loan amount by 300 yuan. As the district has achieved good results in handling loans, the increase has been approved.

Your association is the highest body representing the citizens of the concession, and everyone looks forward to it being able to consider the health and happiness of the citizens. Now it is the hot summer season, and people fear epidemics like tigers. Please protest to the Public Works Department again and remove the garbage wood frame as soon as possible." Considering that the road is lined with shops and is a thoroughfare for vehicles and pedestrians, it is even easier to cause an epidemic if it is not moved in this hot weather. In view of the reasons in the letter, we are writing to you, hoping that you will investigate and handle the matter to emphasize public health and comfort the expectations of the citizens. We still hope to receive a reply so that we can inform you of the situation."

Mitsui's Case is Postponed for Trial 162

After He Gengxing, the compradore of the Japanese Mitsui 洋行, absconded, he owed the company a huge sum of money. The company sued He's guarantor, Hong Cangting, in the Special District Court. At the opening of the trial, Hong's lawyer, Zhang Rongxi, raised the issue of legal person, arguing that Mitsui had not registered with our country's authorities and had not obtained legal person status, so it had no right to sue. The judge in charge instructed the plaintiff to use two remedies: (1) register the 洋行 with our country's government; (2) sue in the name of a natural person. Yesterday morning was another date for the continued trial. In addition to Okamoto, the plaintiff's agent lawyer added Li Zuyu as a lawyer. First, Okamoto presented the revised complaint, stating that the plaintiff had changed to suing in the name of a natural person: Mitsui Morinosuke, a shareholder of Mitsui 洋行, and Fukushima Kishiji, who was elected by the shareholders as the legal representative in this case. If the defendant had no objection to the point of correcting the complaint, please proceed with the trial immediately. Hong's lawyer, Zhang Rongxi, then rose to declare that he admitted that the plaintiff had the ability to sue. The judge in charge then ordered that the case be investigated. Then, Wang Zijian, the lawyer appointed by the court to defend the defendant He Gengxing, stated that after my lawyer was appointed by the court, He's brother, He Xiaobiao, also came to appoint me. Xiaobiao intends to find his younger brother and bring him back to discuss a comprehensive solution with the creditors. The plaintiff's lawyer had previously said that there was hope for reconciliation. Therefore, according to the provisions of Article 193 of the Civil Procedure Law, he requested that the trial be postponed. The plaintiff's lawyer expressed his opposition, saying that reconciliation could also be carried out during the trial. Finally, the judge in charge ruled that the case would be postponed for trial. Then, the trial of Mitsui's lawsuit against Yao Weirong, He Gengxing, Hong Cangting, Zhang Chunlai, Zhang Xingchu, etc. of the Yibi Tongsheng Money Shop for not paying 147,429 taels and one qian was continued. The plaintiff's complaint has also been revised, changing the name to Mitsui Morinosuke, etc. The plaintiff's lawyer, Li Zuyu, requested that the court order the liquidator of the shop, Lawyer Hu Yongde, to submit all the account books for preservation, because there were rumors that the shop would destroy evidence. Therefore, he asked that the books be submitted to stop the rumors. However, according to Lawyer Hu, the account books of the shop were sent by its manager, Zhang Chunlai, but there were no shareholder books, so he could not name the shareholders. The judge in charge then asked how many account books there were. Hu said that there were about 48 books. Lawyer Li further stated that if there was no shareholder book during the liquidation, then it would not be possible to know the amount of the share capital. Since the amount of the share capital was not known, how could the liquidation be carried out? This was very strange. Then, the judge in charge ordered Lawyer Hu to submit all the account books within three days. Chen Tingrui, the representative lawyer of the defendant Yao Weirong, stated that the plaintiff's complaint was too simple. What qualifications did he recognize Yao as? Whether he was a shareholder of the shop, or an issuer, or a guarantor, all were not stated. And the origin of the 16 banknotes sued for was also not detailed, only saying "obtained in good faith", which seemed too general and should be stated in detail. The judge in charge then ordered the plaintiff to submit a detailed complaint to the court and wait for the defendants to be served before setting another date for trial.

Mitsui's Registration Issue 163

Not Completely Confirmed

Mitsui 洋行's case against He Hong for the price of goods was tried in the Special District Court yesterday. Mitsui 洋行 changed to suing in the names of shareholders Mitsui Yasunosuke and Manager Fukushima Kishiji. After the presiding judge asked Zhang Yaoceng, the defendant's representative lawyer, whether he had any objections, Zhang said that he had no objection to suing in the name of a natural person. After the court adjourned, someone asked Zhang Lawyer why. Zhang said that what I raised last time was the issue of the capacity of a general party. Those who have no capacity to have rights according to law have no capacity to be a party, so a company that is not registered cannot be the plaintiff or defendant. Those who have the capacity to have rights have the capacity to be a party, so all natural persons can be the plaintiff or defendant. This time, Mitsui 洋行 changed to using Mitsui Yasunosuke, etc. as the plaintiff. Since Mitsui Yasunosuke is a natural person, he naturally has the capacity to have rights and cannot be said to have no capacity to be a party according to law. Moreover, it is following the court's judgment and correcting it himself. The reason why I stated that there was no objection was to express that there was no objection to this general capacity to be a party. However, whether Mitsui Yasunosuke is a proper party in the legal relationship in dispute in this case, and whether he has the proper rights, is another issue. In other words, whether Mitsui Yasunosuke has the qualification to litigate in this case, that is, whether he is fit to be a party, is another major issue that must be resolved according to law at the beginning of the debate in this case. I originally intended to raise the defense of lack of fitness of the party immediately after the debate began today, and request the court to make an intermediate judgment first. Unexpectedly, the adjournment was announced without debate, so I had to wait until the next time to raise it. Therefore, whether the legal relationship in this case can be litigated by Mitsui Yasunosuke, etc. is still subject to legal resolution. Outsiders do not understand, or think that there is no problem with the parties in this case, and Mitsui 洋行 does not need to register and can litigate this case by other means. This is to misunderstand the distinction between the capacity to be a party and the fitness of a party, and to make a hasty judgment.

Residents of Hengsha Suffer Tragic Disaster in Hurricane and Giant Waves 168

More than 100 Residents Drowned by Inundating Tide

Houses Collapsed and Belongings Washed Away Without a Trace

The area of Hengsha (belonging to the jurisdiction of Chuansha County), located eighty or ninety miles offshore of the Sanjiashui Estuary of Wusong, faces the sea, surrounded by water on all sides. The terrain is low and the coastline is boundless. The residents of the sandbank have built dikes for protection. The northeast hurricane erupted the day before yesterday, with giant waves reaching the sky and the tide suddenly rising more than ten feet. In the low-lying areas behind the sandbank town, the earthen dikes suddenly collapsed and were washed away. The tide poured in, turning the area into a vast swamp. More than a hundred nearby residents were unable to escape and drowned on the spot. Countless houses collapsed and furniture and belongings were washed away without a trace. Most pitifully, a certain family of seven, including men, women, the old, and the young, all drowned, leaving not even chickens or dogs, a truly tragic event.

Ships Involved in Accidents in the Huangpu River During the Wind and Rain the Night Before Last 169

Injured: Sunk Ships: Lost Cargo

The hurricane struck the night before last, becoming more intense in the middle of the night, accompanied by heavy rain. Many cargo ships heavily loaded with goods in the Huangpu River encountered danger. The Tongfeng ship, hired by Hong Yonglin of the Mingguo Road, carrying 200 bales of sesame seeds, was heading to Zhejiang Province. While waiting for the tide to rise for departure, the ship was berthed at Zhoujiadu and was buffeted by the wind and waves, unable to withstand the force. The entire ship capsized, and the crew members fell into the water. Two empty ships berthed nearby heard the shouts for help and rushed to the rescue, rescuing Hong and his crew. However, two other crew members, although not drowned, were seriously injured in the head and back when they collided with iron anchors while escaping to shore. They are currently being treated at the Nanshi Hospital. When the tide receded yesterday, the ship's hull was exposed above the water, leaning to the left. After receiving the report, Tongfeng hired machines to salvage the sunken ship's cargo yesterday. It was reported that the bottom of the ship was damaged by the dredging machine, resulting in significant losses. Furthermore, the Yang Da Zhizhi Pudong ferry ship, loaded with native cloth from Pudong Shengcheng and other companies, was anchored at Lujiahui in the South Huangpu of Pudong the night before last when it was overturned by the wind. The whereabouts of two crew members are currently unknown, presumed to have drowned. Additionally, a Ningbo firewood boat, fully loaded with Hangzhou firewood, capsized in Longhua Bay the night before last due to the wind, resulting in the loss of cargo worth over four thousand yuan. Also, the Shan Heshang Pudong kiln cargo ship, fully loaded with kiln goods, was berthed at the Nanshi Cement Plant pier. During the intense wind, the ship's main mast was blown off and crushed Shan's right arm and the back of a crew member. They were sent to the hospital for treatment. Shan was unharmed and discharged from the hospital on the spot, while his crew member was hospitalized due to severe injuries. It was also reported that a flour boat at the south entrance of Wusong was completely submerged by the wind and waves. Furthermore, many empty ships berthed at the pier had their oars and other equipment blown off by the wind.

Record of the Fire on Manzhou Road, Zhabei 170

Fire Spreads to Coal and Kerosene Stacks

At around 3:50 PM yesterday, a fire suddenly broke out in the Xie Xinxiang coal stack on Manzhou Road near the Guoqing Road intersection in Zhabei. Because the storage consisted of flammable materials, and the wind fueled the fire, the flames quickly spread to the neighboring Dachangsheng stack and six shikumen houses in Chengde Lane (a lane behind). The fire was raging and had not been extinguished for four hours, causing considerable damage. The details obtained from the interview are compiled as follows:

Origin of the Fire: The Xie Xinxiang stack, located at 84 Manzhou Road, was established by Ni Qingsheng from Ningbo. It occupies a large area of approximately one mu and has a monthly rent of seventy-seven yuan. It specializes in storing coal and the business is quite good. Currently, there are a large number of coal and kerosene stockpiles belonging to four companies: Ruitai, Hengfeng, Weichang, and Li Xiexing, Ren Wanyou, totaling approximately seven to eight hundred boxes. At 3:45 PM yesterday, a wisp of green smoke suddenly emerged from the Ruitai kerosene stack. At that time, the old clerk was moving goods and was unaware of the fire. After a while, sparks flew and smoke billowed. An old clerk named Shen Laohu saw the scene and was shocked, running into the street and shouting "Fire!" But the fire had already spread beyond control. According to reports, the cause of the fire was a spark entering a box. The oil tanks in the kerosene stack were stacked very high. The muddy ground was damp, and moisture seeped in, causing rust and leaks in the boxes. Ruitai Oil Stack hired workers to repair them by sealing them with tin. During the work yesterday afternoon, a worker accidentally dropped a spark of melted tin into a box. The kerosene caught fire and exploded in an instant. The worker saw the situation was bad and fled immediately, causing a major disaster.

Spread of the Fire: After the fire broke out, the local fire brigade of the fourth district was the first to arrive with their vehicles, dividing up to connect water hoses and pour water to extinguish the fire. Subsequently, the second and third sections and the fire trucks from the concession, Nanshi, East, West, and South Districts, and the Hujia Muqiao area also arrived one after another. However, the materials stored in the stack were all fuels and difficult to extinguish. In an instant, the fire spread to Dachangsheng stack at 95 to 100 on the left side, and the fire became even more intense. The Dachangsheng stack was larger than Xie Xinxiang, and the materials stored there were also coal briquettes, asphalt, and other similar materials. Moreover, the wind was howling and the water supply was lacking, making it difficult to cope. Then, chemical water was sprayed, and the fire was slightly suppressed.

Fire Damage: During the height of the fire, the Public Security Bureau of the fourth district and the Wuzhen Road Police Station dispatched police to the scene to suppress the situation. The owner of Xie Xinxiang was detained for questioning. It was reported that the stack was not insured. The fire burned the Dachangsheng stack and six houses at 6, 12, 18, 19, 20, and 21 Chengde Lane behind the stack. The estimated loss is no less than tens of thousands of yuan.

Negotiations on the Installation of Electric Poles Beyond the Boundary in Western Shanghai 171

Columbia Road in Western Shanghai is one of the roads built beyond the boundary. It stretches more than three li from Hongqiao Road in the south to Daxi Road in the north. Xu Yan, the director of the second branch of the sixth district of the local Municipal Public Security Bureau, presented a request to Director Yuan in light of the loss of national sovereignty to establish police stations at Hongqiao Road and Daxi Road. However, at around 11:00 AM on the 28th of this month, the British Public Works Department dispatched many armed Chinese police officers accompanied by fourteen Russians to erect electric poles in the middle section of Columbia Road, Anhe Temple Road (i.e., Fahua Road). Wang Zhentang, a patrol officer from the Daxi Road sub-station, and patrol leader Zhou Yida led police officers on patrol and immediately stepped forward to stop the work. The police officers initially refused to stop, stating that they were acting on orders. Wang explained that the land belonged to the Chinese territory, but the road was built by the Public Works Department beyond the boundary. All construction and administrative powers were under the jurisdiction of the Chinese authorities. As Chinese citizens, they should understand the greater righteousness and immediately stop working, pending serious negotiations between their superiors and the relevant consul. Until a resolution was reached, all work should be stopped, otherwise they would be disarmed and enforcement would be carried out forcibly. The police officers then withdrew. As of yesterday, the Jing'an Temple Police Station dispatched armed double-post Chinese police officers to stand guard in front of the police station at both the north and south ends of Columbia Road, in what seemed like surveillance. Director Xu Yan has reported the situation to Director Yuan, who in turn reported it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, arguing based on reason to protect sovereignty.

Negotiations Between the Oil Cake Industry and the Dalian Factory 172

The Shanghai South Oil Cake Industry's various businesses suffered losses last year due to the insufficient weight and inferior quality of the Dalian cakes sold in various inland ports. The cakes were returned to Shanghai or discounted, causing significant damage to the industry. The association requested a ban and convened a meeting of industry members to discuss countermeasures and establish regulations. However, the weight of the Dalian cakes shipped this year is even lighter than before, and the quality is even worse. The industry discovered this and was preparing to organize a review committee when it coincided with the summer season. At a time when farmland in various rural areas was in need, the demand for soybean cakes in Shanghai was high, with approximately five to six thousand cakes being shipped to various ports every day. However, the weight of the cakes delivered by various ships was reduced, causing great indignation among the industry. A general meeting was convened a few days ago to resolve that if inferior or underweight cakes were found again, the industry would stop picking them up and report to the association to negotiate with the merchants who sold them and pursue compensation for losses. Currently, the association is in negotiations. Recently, the weight of the cakes shipped has continued to be reduced, and the cakes have been sent to the association for negotiation. Yesterday, the various businesses met and decided that Dalian cakes were being shipped to Shanghai for sale under false pretenses, causing damage to the industry. The association has repeatedly negotiated to prevent underweight cakes from being shipped under false pretenses, but the Dalian manufacturers have disregarded their credibility and violated the industry's regulations. Currently, the only option is to stop shipments and pursue compensation for losses, which must be resolved before trading with the merchants again. The association has now warned the Dalian manufacturers.

Record of the Special District Court Burning Narcotics 173

This is the First Time in the Special District

Representatives from All Sectors Participated

The Special District Local Court burned the narcotics such as opium, red pills, and other toxins confiscated in cases from April 1 to June 30 at the Yizhong land of the Tongren Baoan Hall on the south side of the court yesterday morning at 10:00 AM. This was the first time this had been done in the concession area. Prior to the event, Court President Yang Zhaoyun sent invitations to various party and government agencies in the local area, as well as the Bar Association and other organizations, inviting them to send representatives to the site to supervise, in order to show prudence. After 7:00 AM yesterday morning, the court ordered workers to construct a long reed mat shed in the center of the Yizhong land, with a long table inside, more than twenty seats and teaware. The site for the burning was about two zhang away from the shed and was circular, with lush green grass that had been mowed and paved with bricks. At 10:30 AM, everything was ready. Court President Yang and Chief Prosecutor Zhou Xianjue led their subordinates to the site, and Xu Weizhen, President of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, also led several prosecutors from the court to the site to supervise. Soon, representatives from various agencies arrived one after another. The Public Works Department also sent legal advisors Mr. Bolang and Mr. Gan Jingxian to visit. They were all received by Court President Yang and Chief Prosecutor Zhou and invited to take their seats. President Xu, dressed in Western attire, sat in the center, and the other guests sat in order. Court police officers were present to maintain order, and outside the site, special Chinese and Western police officers and Indian mounted patrols were dispatched by the local police station to patrol the perimeter wall of the Yizhong land. Initially, some people perched on the top of the wall to watch, but the patrolling police officers, considering it obstructive to order, persuaded them to leave one by one. Four guards were stationed at the entrance of the site, and all those entering were questioned. In total, no less than thirty or forty Chinese and Western individuals and reporters attended to observe. When the burning order was issued, Prosecutor Guo Huaipu and Secretary Ge Sixun first checked the opium paste, opium equipment, red pills, and other narcotics package by package. Any larger packages were opened and inspected in public, and then cut open with knives by the workers. Then, they were moved to the burning site. After the firewood was ignited and the flames were raging, the narcotics were thrown into the fire, and salt was shoveled into the fire, followed by kerosene, which further intensified the flames. At this time, many of those who came to take photos were engaged in photographic work. From 11:00 AM to 1:00 PM, the valuable narcotics were completely reduced to ashes. The supervisors and observers then departed.

Siberian Mail Delivered to Shanghai by Dalian Split Into Two Rounds 174

According to a notice from the postal authorities, the Dalian Post Office divided the Siberian mail destined for Shanghai on the 29th of this month into two rounds of transportation, one on the Dalian Maru and the other on the Changsha Maru. The former carried 182 bags and the latter carried 243 bags.

Opening of the Appeal Hearing in the Zhang Wenqing Matricide Case 175

Zhang Wenqing's Testimony Changes

Chen Hengcai Appeals for Death

Zhang Wenqing, in collusion with Chen Hengcai, the son of a servant, gathered Yao Shuigui and Gao Jintang and murdered his stepmother Zhang Su on the premises of 742 Carter Road in January of this year. After the police arrested and interrogated the perpetrators, a verdict was reached after more than a dozen interrogations, and each of the perpetrators was sentenced to death. The convicts were not willing to accept this and hired lawyers to file an appeal. At 8:30 AM yesterday morning, Song Yuan, the presiding judge of the Criminal Division of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, and two judges, Ye Du, opened the court to summon witnesses and order Zhang and the other three to be brought to the case. Chief Prosecutor Wang Zhennan also attended the court to perform his duties. First, the appellant Zhang Wenqing was interrogated. According to his statement, the deceased stepmother Su was close to being romantic in her everyday behavior, frequently going out and not returning home at night. Chen Hengcai came to my house last winter and told me that he had already arranged for two people to stab Su, because his mother had originally worked as a servant in my house but had been fired by Su. When I heard Chen's remarks, I stopped him for fear of being framed. Judge Song instructed him, "From what you have said, it is clear that you have a special relationship with Chen, otherwise Chen would not have revealed this secret, and if you had no relationship, you would have reported him." Zhang insisted that he had nothing to do with Chen, and said that Chen might have some involvement with Su, because Chen went to Su's room every morning, and apart from Su and her two children, there was no one else in the room. Chen stayed in the room for one or two hours before coming out. Judge Song further instructed him, "Your statement is inconsistent with the previous one, and the meaning of today's words is to protect Chen and cover up your own guilt. In fact, this kind of testimony is of no benefit to you. You should be frank, because what can be determined in this case is the fact that you instigated the crime, but the relationship between you and Chen, the relationship between you and Su, and the relationship between Su and Chen, have not been clarified." Zhang replied that he had no relationship with them, but Chen went to Su's room in the morning. Then the court ordered the bailiff to bring Chen Hengcai to the court from the waiting room. According to Chen's statement, the murder of Su was entirely done by me. Zhang, Yao, and Gao had nothing to do with it and were innocent. I beg that the three men be released and that I be allowed to pay for my crimes. Please execute me quickly. The court instructed him, "The purpose of your appeal is to reduce the sentence of the first trial, but now you want to be sentenced to death, which is not the purpose of the appeal." Chen replied that this was what I wanted to do, so I appealed. In short, Su was actually stabbed by me. After being arrested, I also falsely accused Zhang Wenqing because Zhang Wenqing slandered me. Then Yao Yonggui was brought in for questioning. He stated that he had been implicated. Chen Hengcai had asked him to go to Zhang's house, saying it was for fun, and did not mention murder. When I arrived, Zhang Wenqing was by the handrail. I followed Chen and Gao into the house. Zhang's lawyer Jiang Rong asked Yao, "What did Zhang do when he was by the handrail?" Yao replied that he did not pay attention. Gao Jintang was also questioned, and Gao completely denied participating in the murder. Zhang Jinbao and Yinbao, the two sons of the deceased, testified that when their mother was murdered, they were in the lane. When they returned home, Gao Yonggui opened the door, and Zhang Wenqing was also going upstairs. The court then questioned Zhang Wenqing and Chen Hengcai whether they had opened the door when they entered the house. Zhang denied it. The court then instructed Zhang Wenqing and the others to be returned to custody separately and scheduled to begin the debate this morning.

Old Man Beats Daughter-in-Law to Death 176

Mute Husband Watches Wife Die

Old Father Speaks Up for Daughter

Shi Changhe, a boatman from Yancheng, Jiangbei, berthed his boat at Xiaoshadu. He had a son named Shi Hongcai, who was thirty-six years old and mute. He married Wang Rugang's daughter from the same village and industry. Wang was thirty-four years old this year and had a daughter named Fengying, who was twelve years old this year. However, Shi Changhe had a violent temper, so Shi Wang was often abused. On the thirteenth of this month, Shi Wang became thirsty and asked her daughter to bring tea. The daughter did not obey, and Shi Wang angrily beat her. Unexpectedly, this angered Shi Changhe, who tied up Wang and beat her with a stick, causing her head to bleed. Shi died on the seventeenth. Her husband, Shi Hongcai, saw his wife being beaten to death by his father, but because he was mute, he could not speak. So he hastily collected her body and temporarily housed it in the Jiangbei Guild Hall. Yesterday, Wang Rugang came to Shanghai by boat and went to Xiaoshadu to see his daughter. He saw that his granddaughter Shi Fengying was dressed in mourning. He was shocked and asked her what had happened. Fengying told him everything. Wang was furious and immediately took Shi Changhe to the Sixth District Police Station, who transferred him to the Local Court. He was ordered to be detained pending the opening of the coffin for an inquest.

Death by Unwanted Marriage 177

Sailing into the River, Life Given to the Current

Several Suicide Notes Comfort Family Members

Yesterday morning, a young man in Western attire committed suicide by jumping into the river from a sampan. He could not be rescued and died in the river. He left behind farewell letters to his parents, older brother, and sister-in-law, as well as other miscellaneous items. The reason was dissatisfaction with his marriage. The detailed circumstances are as follows:

The brothers both work in the tailoring business. Su Adi, from Pudong, has been working as a ferryman on the Lujiazui ferry in Pudong. His wife lives at home and farms. They have two sons. The elder son, named Zhanglong, and his wife run a Western-style tailoring shop at 28 Bow-machi, Hongo-ku, Tokyo, Japan. The business is quite prosperous. The younger son, named Lufu, is 22 years old and also a Western-style tailor. He was married in December of last year. Lufu considered this marriage not of his own free will, thus planting the seeds of suicide.

The Newlyweds are Like Strangers. Lufu was young and handsome. Apart from working hours, he always wore elegant Western suits when going out. He was a man of refined manners and had absorbed new knowledge. He strongly advocated absolute freedom in marriage. However, his parents were stubborn and believed that their son's marriage was a matter of obedience to their commands. Last year, they arranged a marriage through a matchmaker with a woman surnamed Mou to be his wife. The wedding was scheduled for December. Lufu, who was working with his brother in Japan, returned home upon hearing the news and strongly opposed this marriage, which was not approved by him, before his parents. However, he could not defy their strict orders and reluctantly married. However, the newlyweds were like strangers. As soon as the New Year holiday was over, Lufu left for Japan and did not return for a long time. His wife had no choice but to weep in secret.

Jumping into the River Mid-Stream. After Lufu arrived in Japan, he continued to work at his brother's shop for more than two months. Then, he made an excuse to return to China and rented a place at 390 Ruixing Lane, Weihaiwei Road, in the British Concession. The house was a Western-style tailoring shop, and Lufu worked there. Although his family was near in Pudong, he did not visit. He only informed his parents that he had come to Shanghai and stated his address. From then on, the thought of suicide suddenly arose. According to his suicide note, he once attempted suicide by taking opium at an inn in Changzhou, but failed. Yesterday morning, at around 7 a.m., he went out alone, wearing a gray serge Western suit, in Shanghai. He walked to the Bund pier on Jiujiang Road, hired sampan number 920, and said he wanted to cross the river. When he reached the middle of the river, he placed a straw hat, a small silver coin, two silver dimes, a suicide note (containing farewell letters to his parents and older brother and sister-in-law), and a blank piece of paper in the cabin. He then jumped into the river and immediately sank without a trace. The sampan boatman, Zheng Acai, tried to save him but failed. He then sent the belongings to the water police station for handling.

The Stubborn Father Weeps with Unavailing Regret. The police station received the report and examined the letter. It was addressed to his brother in Japan. In addition to the letters to his parents, older brother, and sister-in-law, it also stated the Shanghai address as 390 Ruixing Lane, Weihaiwei Road, in the British Concession. There was also a note that read: "Please do not report this to my family. Please ask a charitable organization to collect my body," twelve characters in total. The detective chief immediately ordered Chinese detective Huang Songsheng to investigate the address. The landlord stated that his father, Su Adi, was a ferryman in Pudong and volunteered to summon Su to the location. The detective then questioned Su in detail. As soon as Su heard that his son had committed suicide, he burst into tears. He told the detective in detail how the deceased had opposed the marriage and concluded by saying that he never expected him to commit suicide. The detective then ordered Su to go to the police station to explain the situation. The detective chief instructed him to take the belongings with him and to notify him when the body was recovered for collection.

The Suicide Note. The suicide note consisted of six pages in total: three pages addressed to his parents and three pages addressed to his older brother and sister-in-law. They were enclosed in an envelope. The letter addressed to his parents is copied below: (Dear Parents, Your unfilial son is no longer in this world. I will repay your kindness in raising me as a dog or horse in the next life. I hope a charitable organization will collect my body. Please do not grieve for me. I regret that I took six cents worth of opium at an inn in Changzhou and lay there for thirty hours, but I did not die. If I had died then, I would have had some money to pay for a coffin and clothes. For a month, I spent money like water on beer, soda, and ice cream. I knew I should not have done that, but it was my last pleasure. I suppose I have enjoyed all the pleasures of the world, so I feel it is meaningless. Therefore, I have no choice but to commit suicide. I hope that after I am gone, you will not grieve for me. Please forgive me for seeking peace in the underworld. Otherwise, would it not increase my sins? I will tell you the rest in my dreams. I respectfully wish you both good health and hope you take care of yourselves and eat well. Your sinful son, Lufu, bows a hundred times. July 29.)

A Glimpse of the Contents of the Suicide Note. The letter to his older brother and sister-in-law reads as follows: (Brother, I have committed suicide. After I am gone, please do not think of me. The reason for my death is marriage. I die without regret. However, there is no one to collect my body. What should I do? I suppose I have committed many sins and deserve this fate. I hope you will take good care of our parents. Your brother, Lufu, bows. There are three more pages. Please convey them to our parents when you return to China. It would be best if you return to Shanghai as soon as you receive this letter. If our parents are sad, please comfort them. Farewell to my dear brother, sister-in-law, brothers, and sisters. Please do not think of me. I will close my eyes in the underworld.)

Item: Wu Deceives a Widow for Profit 178

Both Men and Women are Sold

Meeting on a Narrow Path, They are Sent to the Authorities

Shen Fu, a woman from Pinghu, is 44 years old. She used to farm in her hometown for a living. After her husband died, she had no one to rely on. She came to Shanghai by boat in April of this year and stayed at her older sister's house at 92 Tiandeng Lane, inside the Datong Gate. She then went to a matchmaking shop run by Wu in Sanpailou, asking to be introduced as a maid. Because she could not find an employer for a while, she often waited at the shop for a good opportunity. One day, she happened to meet Xiang Wu, a woman from Songjiang, who was 51 years old. They got along well after chatting. Wu, thinking that the woman was naive and easily deceived, told her that a family in Songjiang wanted to hire a maid. They needed someone honest and reliable, and the monthly salary would be eight yuan. The woman believed her and was willing to go to Songjiang with her. After arriving in Songjiang, Xiang Wu led her to Chen Futang's house. The woman thought that Chen was the employer, so she stayed there. Later, she realized that something was wrong, so she asked Chen for the reason. Chen told her the truth, saying that he was 36 years old. He had been farming too much and had not yet married because his family was poor. Xiang Wu came here and said that she knew a woman, referring to you, who had no one to rely on after her husband died and wanted to find a suitable person to spend the rest of her life with. She said that if the woman was willing, she only needed to pay sixty yuan to make it happen. He was happy to hear that and obtained sixty yuan from outside. After giving the money, he brought you here. In reality, you are my wife. The woman was shocked to hear this. She knew that she had been deceived by Wu, but what was done could not be undone. She had no choice but to go along with it. After a month, she saw that Chen's family was poor. She also saw that Chen was violent and would scold and beat her. She felt that life was unbearable and difficult to stay. So, she secretly escaped the other day and took a car to Shanghai. She still stayed at her sister's house. Yesterday afternoon, at around 2 p.m., the woman happened to meet Xiang Wu on the road near the Tasi Bridge. Because she had suffered so much after being deceived, she could not let it go. As soon as she saw Wu, she grabbed her and called out to Yan Likui, the guard at the sixth post there. She was taken back to the third section of the first district. After preliminary interrogation by Chief Jin, he found that Xiang Wu's behavior was cunning and that she dared to lure and sell rural women. It was extremely abhorrent. He ordered her to be sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Qu vs. Zhou Grave Dispute: Lawyers Testify 179

The case of Qu Shen, a local woman, and her son Qu Shunxiang, disputing the ancestral grave with Zhou Jianren, was publicly heard by Criminal Judge Shen Bingrong in the local court some days ago. It remained unresolved, with the judge ordering further hearings with witnesses. This was reported in the previous newspaper. Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., Judge Shen opened the First Court again for questioning. The plaintiff's lawyer, Chen Kuitang, and the defendant's lawyer, Ye Fulou, arrived in court one after another. The witnesses for both parties, lawyers Wang Chengkuan and Gu Yongquan, attacked each other in court. The details of the questioning are recorded below. After Judge Shen took the stand, he ordered the witness Su Zuoxian to the case. Su testified, "The draft contract was signed on March 27th, and the settlement agreement was made at the Dafugui Restaurant on May 4th. Zhou Jianren was out for business and appointed me as his representative." (Question) "Did Zhou Jianren hire lawyer Gu Yongquan?" (Answer) "Yes, he did. The other party hired lawyer Wang Chengkuan." (Question) "Were you fully authorized?" (Answer) "Yes, I was fully authorized. At that time, the local guarantor Yu Bingchen said that the Qu family had a lot of evidence. Zhou Jianren instructed me to deal with it carefully. Zhou's intention was to pay at most two or three thousand yuan. When the time came, they wanted six thousand two hundred yuan. Because Yu said that there was a lot of evidence, I agreed." (Question) "How many deeds were there at that time?" (Answer) "Yu Bingchen took out two blank deeds from his side. Then I wrote a note for six thousand two hundred yuan. After it was written, Yu took it away. But before that, Yu Bingchen said that there was a 'fang dan' (square receipt), several 'jue qi' (absolute deeds), and eight years of grain strings. I didn't expect that only two blank deeds would be used when making the agreement." (Question) "Did both lawyers witness this?" (Answer) "Both witnessing lawyers, Wang Chengkuan and Gu Yongquan, saw it." (Question) "Were Zhao Qiming, Zhang Shousan, Yu Bingchen, and others present?" (Answer) "They were all present. There was also an old woman (i.e., Qu Shen)." The witness Gu Yongquan testified, "I am currently a lawyer." (Question) "Were you present for the Qu and Zhou families' land dispute?" (Answer) "I was present." (Question) "How many deeds did the Qu family hand over at that time?" (Answer) "Only two blank deeds. After Su Zuoxian wrote the note, the two blank deeds were taken out of Yu Bingchen's pocket." The witness Liu Guisheng testified, "I run a customs brokerage in Yongji Lane, Jiangxi Road." (Question) "Does Qu Shunxiang have land mortgaged to you?" (Answer) "No, Qu Shunxiang mortgaged the land from the thirtieth year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing dynasty through Qu Shunxiang's father, Qu Xianglin, to my father for three hundred yuan. On April 30th of this year, Qu Xianglin's wife, Qu Shen, came with Zhao Qiming (i.e., Cao Qiming) and others to redeem it for seven hundred yuan." (Question) "How many deeds were there?" (Answer) "Five 'shang shou qi' (first-hand deeds), one 'fang dan' (square receipt), and one mortgage deed, a total of seven deeds." (Question) "Was it Lot 189 of Tanzizhen?" (Answer) "Yes, it was redeemed in my shop." Lawyer Wang Chengkuan testified, "I am a lawyer." (Question) "Did you go to Dafugui on May 4th?" (Answer) "I went. Qu Shen came to entrust me beforehand. By the time we got to Dafugui, they had already negotiated. I drafted the settlement agreement, and Su Zuoxian wrote the note. After the settlement agreement was written, Qu Shen handed over one 'fang dan' (square receipt) and five deeds to Zhao Qiming, who handed them over to me. I then handed them over to the other party's lawyer, Gu Yongquan. Yu Bingchen was overseeing on the side." (Question) "Is this all true?" (Answer) "It is true. How can a lawyer lie?" The interrogator said, "Your testimony is completely inconsistent with Gu Yongquan's testimony. But you are a lawyer, and Gu is also a lawyer. Which one is false and which one is true?" At this point, Gu Yongquan repeatedly said, "Lawyer Wang is too unethical, a disgrace to lawyers!" Judge Shen quickly stopped him, saying, "You are also a lawyer, how can you insult him in court?" Judge Shen asked Wang again, "Why did you only write 'all documents' on the settlement agreement and not specify the types?" (Answer) "This is how Gu Yongquan instructed me to write it, because everything had already been negotiated." Judge Shen then asked Gu Yongquan when the deed was signed. Gu answered, "The deed was signed on May 26th. The owner is Lu Youyuan." Lawyer Wang Chengkuan said, "At 11 a.m. on May 26th, Gu Yongquan and Su Zuoxian came to my office and said to me, 'We are signing the deed today. They want to embezzle the six thousand two hundred yuan that should be paid to the Qu family completely and offered me two thousand yuan, with the rest to be split between them.' I didn't think that was right and expressed my opposition. After Gu left, he came again and told me that the Qu family's money had not been paid. I thought that because the parties were not familiar with the law, they hired a lawyer to testify to ensure legal protection. But in this case, even with a lawyer's testimony, there are more complications. I really didn't expect it!" Judge Shen asked Gu Yongquan again, "Did you and Su go to lawyer Wang's office on May 26th?" (Answer) "I didn't go. I went to Lu Youyuan's house at 10 a.m. and left at 12:45 p.m. At that time, Yu Bingchen wanted to transfer six thousand two hundred yuan to Lu, but Lu refused, saying that the money should be paid directly from the Zhou family to the Qu family." The witness Zhao Qiming testified, "There were indeed six deeds, which were transferred to lawyer Gu." Qu Shunxiang testified, "I had not arrived in Shanghai on May 4th, so my mother Qu Shen went to Dafugui." (Question) "Why is Qu Shen not here today?" (Answer) "She has diarrhea and cannot come to court." (Question) "When did you arrive in Shanghai?" (Answer) "May 10th." At this point, the redeemed mortgage deed was presented to the court. After Judge Shen examined it, he ordered Zhou Jianren to the case and testified, "I didn't go to Dafugui on May 4th because of class. I asked Su Zuoxian to represent me. I only found out later that I was deceived." He also requested the judge to summon the grave keeper Zhao Jinyuan for testimony. Judge Shen then said to both lawyers, "We will not hold arguments today. We will continue to hear witnesses and schedule another hearing." Then he adjourned the court.

Zhang Amu's Misfortunes Never Come Singly 180

Losing His Son and Injuring His Son-in-Law

Zhang Amu, from Ningbo, is currently in his forties and works at the Xie Da Game Shop on Caishi Street in the French Concession. His first wife died early, leaving behind a son and a daughter. He remarried a woman surnamed Mou, and they live together on the third floor of the Ruifengxiang New Clothes Shop opened by the Xiaoningbo family across from Xie Da. His daughter has already married. His son, Hongfa, is currently sixteen years old and is apprenticing at a customs brokerage. The other day, Hongfa had nothing to do at the brokerage and was playing chess with another apprentice. The weather was hot, and they were sweating profusely. The other apprentice (who is ten years old) suggested that Hongfa go to the Huangpu Bund to cool off. At that time, the hot sun had not yet abated. Hongfa wanted the other apprentice to take a cold bath with him. The apprentice was young and timid and hesitated. Hongfa took off his clothes and asked the apprentice to take them. Then he jumped into the Huangpu River. At that time, the tide was high, and the waves were surging. After Hongfa entered the water, he did not surface again and joined the water ghosts. The apprentice waited on the Bund for two or three hours but still did not see Hongfa come ashore. The apprentice had no choice but to take the clothes back to the brokerage and inform the manager, who in turn informed Hongfa's father, Zhang Amu. After receiving the news, he sent someone to inform his son-in-law, planning to go to the Huangpu Bund with him to find his son's body. His son-in-law received the message and immediately left home (near Xiaodongmen). He was attacked by enemies with knives and stabbed several times, fell injured to the ground, and was taken by family members by car to Baolong Hospital for treatment. Zhang's situation can be described as misfortunes never come singly. Currently, his son Hongfa's body has floated up at the Beijing Road Pier and is being prepared for burial. His son-in-law's injuries are not fatal, and his life is not in danger.

Enemy Axes Xue Bingsheng 181

Yesterday afternoon, around 5 p.m., Xue Bingsheng was walking across the street from Fuchang Pawnshop on Zhejiang Road, Guangdong Road, when three or four enemies attacked him with axes, knocking him to the ground. The patrol police from the Laozha Police Station sent the injured man to Renji Hospital. He was seriously injured in the buttocks, arms, and legs.

Chen Qichang Loses a Fortune

French Police Detective Inspector General Shen Defu, Inspector Chen Sanlin, Detective Lu Jinchen, Bao detectives Jiang Changwen, Ni Xiafei

Page 16

and others discovered that there were hidden opium and secret sales in a house at a certain number of Deli on Laobeimen Street, which violated the ban. Bribery Attempt by Detectives Rejected 183

Zheng Zhi, who acted as a bribe-giver on behalf of Hu, was also charged at the same time. Qian Huafo's Buddhist Painting Lawsuit 184

A Friend Sues Him for Degeneration

A Calligrapher Claims to Have Bought It Last Year

Qian Huafo is famous at the time for his good at drawing Buddhist images. In the past, he was good at drama, but in recent years, Qian abandoned the stage life of an actor and became a painter. Zhou Wuming, a Ningbo native and manager of the Yichun Hall fan shop at Paoxiu field on Nanjing Road, allegedly imitated Qian's seal on a Buddhist image painted by someone else and printed it on the image, which infringed on copyright. Qian filed a criminal suit against Zhou for privately making a seal and filed a civil suit to recover losses. Judge Cheng Shangfeng of the Special District Local Court summoned him for trial yesterday morning. According to Qian's confession, he did not know that the defendant had done this. This spring, when he talked about painting with a friend, the friend said that the brushwork of the Buddha he painted was suddenly becoming more and more degenerated, and advised him to abandon this business and seek another livelihood. I asked him what he saw and said that the Buddha statue I saw hanging in Yichun Hall had dull brushwork, how could it be easily sold for money? In March, I asked a friend to buy a Buddha statue from the hall for a price of 22 yuan. Upon closer inspection, I realized that this painting was not my handwriting, it was impersonating my name, a forged seal. So he presented one of the Buddhas he painted to the court, requesting verification. According to the defendant's confession, the Buddha sold to the plaintiff was consigned by a Shen family member, and I only sold it on consignment. I have never been responsible for its authenticity. Shen is also present today. So, according to Shen Youren's confession, the painting was indeed entrusted to the defendant for consignment. I have made a living selling books, and the painting was bought last year for twelve yuan, not painted by myself. When I bought it, I thought it was Huafo's brush, so I wrote a poem on the painting and asked the defendant to sell it on consignment, but I didn't know it was a counterfeit. Judge Cheng ordered a retrial in seven days and sent a bailiff to the defendant's Paichun Hall to retrieve the business books for verification.

Fashionable Girl Caught with Opium 185

A Total of Seventy-Four Packets of Opium

Yesterday morning, around 11:30 a.m., a short-haired woman, wearing a cheongsam and leather shoes, quite fashionable, and carrying a leather bag, looking like a female staff member serving in an agency, was lingering at the Wusong Town Station. Yang Maorong, the seventh district chief of public security, noticed that the woman's behavior was suspicious. He sent detectives Yu Peifa and Ling Zifa to investigate. They saw the woman leave the station in a panic. They stopped her for questioning, but she was evasive. They found a total of seventy-four packets of opium of various sizes in the leather bag. They took the woman to the district. After questioning by District Chief Yang, she confessed that her name was Wang Shengying, 23 years old, from Wusong, and currently works at the Haining Road Telephone Company in Shanghai. The leather bag was entrusted to her by her acquaintance Li Genbao to take to Song, and she didn't know that it contained opium. When he ordered an investigation into Li Genbao, there was no such person. Obviously, the woman was minimizing her responsibility. District Chief Yang, because the case was related to smuggling opium, ordered the suspect to be sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau along with the opium for questioning.

When he arrived at the hotel, he had not yet died, so he was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. But he was too poisoned, and the treatment was ineffective. He died at 6:30 p.m.

Yesterday morning, around 11:30 a.m., in the Di Yi Lou teahouse in the Jiumu area of the city, three or four tea guests wearing short clothes were sitting at a table, sipping tea. They were happily chatting when one of them, a man wearing a blue cloth shirt and trousers, suddenly became ill, bowed his head on the table, and remained silent. In a moment, his face was pale, his eyes were dull, and his limbs were cold. His companions were trying to send him to the hospital for treatment when he suddenly died. The deceased was still sitting on the chair, with his head resting on the back of the chair. For a time, the residents nearby gathered to watch, and everyone was amazed. It is said that the deceased was from Ningbo, came from Zhabei, and was planning to return to Ningbo on a boat in the afternoon. He was about forty years old. The teahouse owner reported it to the police district in charge.

Letters to the Editor 195

To the Editor,

I am writing regarding the item in your newspaper's local news column on July 27 concerning the statistics of patients at the Red Cross Epidemic Hospital, which stated that one percent of patients had genuine cholera. This is inconsistent with the facts. Since our hospital opened on the 10th of this month, although we have treated more than five hundred people, we have never encountered anyone with genuine cholera. However, it is true that one percent of patients received physiological saline infusions, which may have led to the misunderstanding. We request that your newspaper correct this.

Sincerely,

The Chinese Red Cross

July 30th

To the Editor,

I am writing regarding the item on page four of your newspaper on July 29 which stated that Platoon Leader Bu Yunzhou of the First Regiment of the Guard Brigade went to the Longhua Command Headquarters on official business, and that the accompanying military police found that the soldiers accompanying the platoon leader were carrying a bomb, which they threw but did not explode, causing the passengers on the vehicle to be greatly alarmed. Our regiment has checked the roster thoroughly and there is no person named Platoon Leader Bu Yunzhou. Furthermore, no one has been sent to the Longhua Command Headquarters on official business recently. We suspect that the report is inaccurate. We have dispatched investigators to ascertain the truth, and we are sending this letter specifically for correction. We hope that you will publish it in the "Letters to the Editor" column.

Sincerely,

Headquarters, First Regiment, Guard Brigade, National Government

The general practice in ranking creditors is to prioritize them according to the amount owed, with the largest debts coming first. Book and Newspaper Reviews

Sociological Miscellany, Issue 2, Edited by Yang Qi Yun 196

Edited by the Southeast Sociological Society

Published by World Book Company

The second issue of "Sociological Miscellany" contains nine treatises: (1) Two Classifications of Social Action, (2) Sociology and Economics, (3) Research on Rural Social Surveys, (4) A Theory of Sociological Systems, (5) On the Content of Sociology and a Response to Mr. Peng Jixiang, (6) Labor Legislation in China, (7) Culture and Eugenics, (8) Eugenics and Culture, (9) Further Discussion on Culture and Eugenics. A summary introduction is given below:

Two Classifications of Social Action

Society is already complex enough. To study its actions within this complexity, one must analyze and categorize them in detail. The author of this article, Xu Shilian, uses an objective approach, emphasizing the social nature, to propose a classification of actions, demonstrating a path for scholars to study social actions. At the same time, he introduces Professor Hayes' subjective analysis, which emphasizes individual psychology, as a classification of social actions.

From a sociological perspective, any classification has its own advantages and disadvantages. However, subjective classifications, focusing on the internal, tend to have more flaws. Therefore, the author "does not consider civil analysis to be perfect," because psychological analysis lacks actions related to group self-preservation and group perpetuation.

Naturally, the noteworthy aspect of this article lies in the author's objective analysis, which has its own unique insights.

Sociology and Economics

The author is one of China's leading socio-economists, particularly skilled in the study of economic thought. This is mentioned in the editor's preface to this issue. Therefore, the author reveals the original face of an economist. He affirmatively states that economics is an independent science and is not a part of sociology.

The full text is divided into four layers: (1) Is sociology a part of economics, or is economics a part of sociology? (2) Similarities between sociology and economics, (3) What sociological subjects should be studied when studying economics? (4) What economic subjects should be studied when studying sociology?

Regarding the first point, the author begins by saying, "Sociology and economics are both independent sciences, each with its own focus, and each does not hinder the other." From this statement, many proofs are derived, explaining the erroneous arguments of previous scholars, and stating the reasons why economics has become a science. He says that economics studies the relationship between people and wealth, extracting facts and theories related to economics from social sciences to make it a science. The second part discusses "The similarities between sociology and economics." The author tells us there are three points: (1) The greatest similarity between sociology and economics is that both are sciences that study the relationship between people; (2) In terms of methods, the two subjects use the same methods. The methods of deduction and induction are indispensable; (3) Sociology and economics have close relationships with other sciences. In other words, due to the similarity of their content and nature, sciences that are very important to sociologists are also of equal importance to economists. In addition, the last two layers of this article can be said to be where the value of the article lies, showing students the way to study and helping them choose courses.

Research on Rural Social Surveys

China has never seen systematic surveys and accurate statistics on any matter. When studying many social problems in recent times, one often only uses foreign survey research materials to prove the evidence of a certain social problem in China. Isn't this a ridiculous joke that involves cutting wood to fit shoes, and forced analogies? The author of this article recognizes this point. He says, "China has always lacked systematic and organized research in the area of social surveys, especially in the area of rural society. Apart from a few poems by literati and scholars, a few notes by philosophers, or occasional descriptions of the social situation at the time, there is no so-called social survey. Although there are some fragmentary articles now, very few are accurate and in accordance with the principles of survey." At the same time, we know that our China is an agricultural country. If we want to improve the countryside, revitalize agriculture, we must first know what should be reformed and what should be promoted. Therefore, we have no choice but to start with surveys.

This article focuses on discussing the methods of rural social surveys. The author uses scientific methods and, based on rural social phenomena, sets out the procedures and methods of investigation. At the same time, he analyzes the types of rural social surveys into a precise outline, and at the end, he also attaches fourteen types of forms for surveying rural society, which are drafted according to the conditions of Chinese rural society. It can be said to be a very valuable work.

A Theory of Sociological Systems

Sociologists have never had a consistent view on sociological theories. Naturally, everyone has their own system. The author of this article first describes the general classifications, including those of Ward, Endo Ryukichi, Shinmei Seido, and other sociological system classifications. In the final section, he writes out "Our Classification of Sociological Systems." The author believes that Comte's efforts in the history of modern sociology have resulted in two main sociological systems: (1) comprehensive sociological systems and (2) sociological systems of special social sciences.

The entire text can be said to be of an introductory nature. As the editor's preface says, "The collection is very rich, and the views are especially appropriate." I naturally also admit the first point, but the second sentence "The views are especially appropriate" is contrary to my observation. I feel that this article seems to lack some insights and does not explain the gains and losses of each "classification of systems."

Labor Legislation in China

Although my country's industry is still very immature, the labor disputes in our major cities are already quite considerable. If we want to reduce labor disputes and increase work efficiency, we naturally need complete labor laws. The author of this article, Zhu Jun, has collected all the labor laws and regulations in China's history to make a systematic analysis and critique. In the draft factory law proposed by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in the 17th year of the Republic of China, the section on surplus distribution is very noteworthy. Even the Chinese Economic Society held a research conference at Nanjing Central University to discuss it. The author's opinion is that "According to this kind of suspension question, it is extremely relevant to China's industry. It cannot be promulgated rashly without detailed research from both theoretical and factual aspects. Because China's industry is being destroyed by imperialism, it is always in a precarious situation. The development of industry should be promoted as much as possible, so that unemployed workers can find work."

The last part of this article is where the author's views are most appropriate. He says that there are two key points in compiling labor laws: (1) When compiling labor laws, one must distinguish the theoretical basis. The author believes that my country's labor laws "should pay attention to the increase of production, and promote labor-management cooperation. In short, Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Principle of People's Livelihood should be the theoretical basis of labor law." (2) When compiling labor laws, one must first investigate the current state of society. Building cars behind closed doors will naturally not be applicable. The author tells us that "Law is a solution to cure social diseases. The theory only explains the method of dispensing medicine, so in clinical practice, it is impossible to start without detailed observation of the symptoms." The above two points are very worthy of attention by legislators.

The Question of "Culture and Eugenics"

Regarding this question, there are three articles in this issue of "Sociological Miscellany". The first is Sun Benwen's "Culture and Eugenics", which was originally published in the third issue of the first volume of the "Social Science Magazine". Because it aroused Pan Guangdan's debate, it is reprinted here. After Mr. Sun wrote that article "Culture and Eugenics", it aroused Mr. Pan's debate, and he wrote an article "Eugenics and Culture". Then Mr. Sun wanted to rebut, so he wrote another article "Further Discussion on Culture and Eugenics".

We know that Mr. Pan is a eugenicist, and Mr. Sun is a cultural sociologist. He is very opposed to the so-called "psychological inheritance" theory. Naturally, the two of them stand in absolutely opposite positions in academic views. In this way, as the editor said, "I hope that the question of culture and eugenics can become clearer with more debate." The two debated purely from an academic standpoint, each with sufficient basis, criticizing each other, and blaming each other. We naturally admit that, especially in the era when our country's academics are immature, this kind of academic superstitious attitude has considerable value. However, because basic sociology is the most belated science, as for eugenics and cultural sociology, which are still in their infancy, it is difficult for us to say who is right and who is wrong. In short, each is a faithful believer, and each person's words can represent the theories of each school, and they are doing their best to advocate that the theories of each school are correct and scientific. Naturally, it is very worthwhile for us to explore together. Here, we hope that a third party can publish a powerful theory on this issue from an objective attitude.

Publication of Vanguard Weekly, Issue 6 197

The Vanguard Weekly, published by the Vanguard Society, was originally scheduled to be published on Sunday. Its sixth issue was delayed until yesterday due to the relocation of the printing house. The main items include: (1) The Mission of Nationalist Literature (Part II), (2) Our Own People (poetry), (3) Talking Points: A. 606, B. Red-Headed Ah San, C. To the Red and Green Literati, (4) Two Orphans, all of which are very exciting, especially the mission of nationalist literature and the works of Pan Sitong of the Talk about White Goose Painting Society.

606 is the most eye-catching. The new poem "Our Own People" was misprinted and could not be corrected. It will be reprinted in the seventh issue. The seventh issue will still be published on schedule on Sunday. The sales offices in Shanghai include Kaiming, Zhenmei, Shanxin Shengming, Jinwu, Daguang, Modern Guanghua bookstores, and major bookstores in other cities.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Reviews 198

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc. books and newspapers are included in the introduction, but boring books will not be introduced.

The pictures are limited to new works by new writers at home and abroad and attached pictures related to the text.

(2) Texts on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(3) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(4) Each text should not exceed 3,000 words at most.

Page 19

The Story of World Literature (184) 199

By American John Macy, translated by Hu Zhongchi

Chapter 48 American Essays and History

Many extremely magnificent writers are famous in more than one department of literature. From this point of view, classifying writers as essayists, poets, novelists, etc. is somewhat far-fetched and does not conform to the human spirit. In short, Poe, whom we consider in more detail as a poet and storyteller, belongs to the first-class essayist. Those who consider some of Poe's essays and "essays" as the most brilliant moments of his extraordinary talent, I do not want to argue with them.

Poe's short and bumpy life was slightly warmed by the reputation of being a journalist and the fact that his actual good achievements were partially recognized. Emerson followed his clear path as an informal pastor. Thoreau lived mostly alone, making a living with pencils. His essays often touched on public issues, but he never actually participated in those issues. Whatever was enjoyed, in short, two essayists from New England enjoyed a more glorious life in the world, namely Lowell and Holmes.

Holmes was a doctor, a professor of anatomy at Harvard Medical School, and an aristocrat from Boston who built a mansion on Beacon Street. He knew the art of composing light poems fluently with his wit, but the gods did not want him to become a poet. The gods made him an essayist, an extremely excellent essayist, with a pleasant, slow pace and a variety of endless materials. "The Autocrat of the Breakfast Table" is as fresh today as it was when it was published in "The Atlantic Monthly" more than sixty years ago. It gives Holmes the qualifications to be ranked alongside Montaigne and Lamb. As Lowell cleverly commented on him, he was endowed with "the great preservative of fame, namely style."

Moreover, Lowell himself has a talent for prose that rings much more surely in my ears than his delicate talent in poetry. Lowell was a well-bred man, a professor of literature at Harvard University, but certainly not a scholar. He was the minister sent from the United States to England, and a man of considerable influence at the time. His range of interests was wide. His Chaucer essay is the best there is. And when the world was still skeptical about that incredible figure from Illinois, and conservative politicians gave advice that later proved to be an overestimation, Lowell understood Lincoln and with decisive wisdom "estimated his value." Regarding the only part of his poetry that I believe still has vitality, I will talk about it soon. Here, I will only mention the extremely humorous, extremely Yankee-style essay "A Certain Condescension in Foreigners."

America is extremely rich in the makers of history, or the authors of history, who know the method of their own expression. The makers of history with the talent for speech or writing are Franklin, Jefferson, Webster, Lincoln, etc. Other readers will immediately add something to my choice - if we can separate one department of human thought from another - is determined not by political historical judgment, but by purely literary standards.

Franklin's "Autobiography" and his occasional essays and letters may not be things of high value in literary history, but they depict an upright and humorous character in a neat tone, and because Franklin, a practical figure who can be regarded as a "efficiency expert" today, studied Addison's "Spectator" in order to complete his own writing style, he also retains his own strong personality. Also, it has a special literary interest.

Jefferson's national documents and correspondence have more than just historical interest. Whether he was bizarrely wrong or extraordinarily correct in his political theory and practice is not a question for us now. He had a shadow of an artist in his nature. The "Declaration of Independence" he drafted is a model of clear and eloquent wording.
